                        cas_cit1R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">1</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrode materials for rechargeable sodium-ion batteries: potential alternatives to current lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Sung-Wook; Seo, Dong-Hwa; Ma, Xiaohua; Ceder, Gerbrand; Kang, Kisuk</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2012</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">2</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">710-721</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADEMBC</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1614-6840</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Lithium (Li)-ion batteries (LIB) have governed the current worldwide rechargeable battery market due to their outstanding energy and power capability.  In particular, the LIB's role in enabling elec. vehicles (EVs) has been highlighted to replace the current oil-driven vehicles in order to reduce the usage of oil resources and generation of CO2 gases.  Unlike Li, sodium is one of the more abundant elements on Earth and exhibits similar chem. properties to Li, indicating that Na chem. could be applied to a similar battery system.  In the 1970s-80s, both Na-ion and Li-ion electrodes were investigated, but the higher energy d. of Li-ion cells made them more applicable to small, portable electronic devices, and research efforts for rechargeable batteries have been mainly concd. on LIB since then.  Recently, research interest in Na-ion batteries (NIB) has been resurrected, driven by new applications with requirements different from those in portable electronics, and to address the concern on Li abundance.  In this article, both neg. and pos. electrode materials in NIB are briefly reviewed.  While the voltage is generally lower and the vol. change upon Na removal or insertion is larger for Na-intercalation electrodes, compared to their Li equiv., the power capability can vary depending on the crystal structures.  It is concluded that cost-effective NIB can partially replace LIB, but requires further investigation and improvement.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGonnrfiSUpaRrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljDk3U-W5Y77w"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XhtVOrtLjF&amp;md5=485b20393bb8876b2f69ca708aeba606</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref2'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit2" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201410376"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kundu, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Talaie, E.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Duffort, V.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Nazar, L.                 10.1002/anie.201410376</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D54%26publication_year%3D2015%26pages%3D3431-3448%26journal%3DAngew.%2BChem.%252C%2BInt.%2BEd.%26issue%3D11%26author%3DD.%2BKundu%26author%3DE.%2BTalaie%26author%3DV.%2BDuffort%26author%3DL.%2BF.%2BNazar%26title%3DThe%2BEmerging%2BChemistry%2Bof%2BSodium%2BIon%2BBatteries%2Bfor%2BElectrochemical%2BEnergy%2BStorage%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fanie.201410376&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.6b12529&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fanie.201410376&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit2R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">2</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">The Emerging Chemistry of Sodium Ion Batteries for Electrochemical Energy Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kundu, Dipan; Talaie, Elahe; Duffort, Victor; Nazar, Linda F.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">54</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3431-3448</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review of some of the current scientific issues underpinning sodium-ion batteries.  Cathode and anode materials and electrolytes for high-performance sodium-ion batteries as well as computational studies of sodium ion mobility are discussed.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrXjTRqIj7rwrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhWXlvdzpDiJQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXjslCiurs%253D&amp;md5=ef99bad4dc7a644dfa380894720626ed</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref3'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit3" data-doi="10.1021/acs.chemmater.5b00869"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Nam, K. W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kim, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, E.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jung, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Levi, E.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Aurbach, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Choi, J. W.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Critical Role of Crystal Water for a Layered Cathode Material in Sodium Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Chem. Mater.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">27</span><span class="NLM_x"> (</span><span class="NLM_issue">10</span><span class="NLM_x">) </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">3721</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">3725</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit3R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">3</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Critical Role of Crystal Water for a Layered Cathode Material in Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Nam, Kwan Woo; Kim, Sangryun; Yang, Eunjeong; Jung, Yousung; Levi, Elena; Aurbach, Doron; Choi, Jang Wook</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Layered transition metal oxides are considered promising cathodes for sodium ion batteries (SIBs) due to their superior specific capacities.  However, they usually suffer from insufficient cycling and rate performance mainly from the structural instability during repeated cycles.  These longstanding challenges are overcome by engaging crystal water in the interlayer space of sodium manganese oxide under the Birnessite framework.  The crystal water enhances Na ion diffusion both in the crystal host and at the interface, suppresses fatal Mn2+ dissoln., and improves long-term structural stability, leading to excellent performance in rate capability and cycle life.  The current study suggests that many hydrated materials can be good candidates for electrode materials of emerging rechargeable batteries that need to deal with the large size or multivalent charge of their carrier ions.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGorAuRErefm87Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhWXlvdzpDiJQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXnvFClsrw%253D&amp;md5=c97f9664dda9f15a0a6d53fd9366b614</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref4'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit4" data-doi="10.1021/acs.jpclett.5b00868"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Dall’Agnese, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Taberna, P.-L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gogotsi, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Simon, P.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Two-Dimensional Vanadium Carbide (MXene) as Positive Electrode for Sodium-Ion Capacitors</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.                         cas_cit4R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">4</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Two-Dimensional Vanadium Carbide (MXene) as Positive Electrode for Sodium-Ion Capacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Dall'Agnese, Yohan; Taberna, Pierre-Louis; Gogotsi, Yury; Simon, Patrice</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Physical Chemistry Letters</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Ion capacitors store energy through intercalation of cations into an electrode at a faster rate than in batteries and within a larger potential window.  These devices reach a higher energy d. compared to electrochem. double layer capacitor.  Li-ion capacitors are already produced com., but the development of Na-ion capacitors is hindered by lack of materials that would allow fast intercalation of Na-ions.  Here the electrochem. behavior is investigated of 2D vanadium carbide, V2C, from the MXene family.  We investigated the mechanism is investigated of Na intercalation by XRD and achieved capacitance of ∼100 F/g at 0.2 mV/s.                         cas_cit5R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">5</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Flexible Membranes of MoS2/C Nanofibers by Electrospinning as Binder-Free Anodes for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xiong, Xiaoqin; Luo, Wei; Hu, Xianluo; Chen, Chaoji; Qie, Long; Hou, Dongfang; Huang, Yunhui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Scientific Reports</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A flexible membrane consisting of MoS2/carbon nanofibers has been fabricated by a simple electrospinning method.  MoS2 nanosheets are uniformly encapsulated in the inter-connected carbon nanofibers with diams. of ∼150 nm.  When evaluated as a binder-free electrode for sodium-ion batteries, the as-obtained electrode demonstrates high performances, including high reversible capacity of 381.7 mA h g-1 at 100 mA g-1 and superior rate capability (283.3, 246.5 and 186.3 mA h g-1 at 0.5, 1 and 2 A g-1, resp.).                         cas_cit6R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">6</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High cyclability of carbon-coated TiO2 nanoparticles as anode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ge, Yeqian; Jiang, Han; Zhu, Jiadeng; Lu, Yao; Chen, Chen; Hu, Yi; Qiu, Yiping; Zhang, Xiangwu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">157</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Owing to the merits of good chem. stability, elemental abundance and nontoxicity, TiO2 (TiO2) has drawn increasing attraction for use as anode material in Na-ion batteries.  Nanostructured TiO2 was able to achieve high energy d.  However, nanosized TiO2 is typically electrochem. instable, which leads to poor cycling performance.  To improve the cycling stability, C from thermolysis of poly(vinyl pyrrolidone) was coated onto TiO2 nanoparticles.  Electronic cond. and electrochem. stability were enhanced by coating C onto TiO2 nanoparticles.  The resultant C-coated TiO2 nanoparticles exhibited high reversible capacity (242.3 mAh g-1), high coulombic efficiency (97.8%), and good capacity retention (87.0%) at 30 mA g-1 over 100 cycles.  By comparison, untreated TiO2 nanoparticles showed comparable reversible capacity (237.3 mAh g-1) and coulombic efficiency (96.2%), but poor capacity retention (53.2%) under the same condition.  The rate performance of C-coated TiO2 nanoparticles was also displayed ≤127.6 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 800 mA g-1.  The improved cycling performance and rate capability were mostly attributed to protective C layer helping stabilize solid electrolyte interface formation of TiO2 nanoparticles and improving the electronic cond.  Therefore, C-coated TiO2 nanoparticles are promising anode candidate for Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqcVSv_A0qWyrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgwpvnezl0JEw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtlOnurg%253D&amp;md5=845e991863dbb9108adc17af6da9f7f0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref7"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref7'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">7</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit7" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2015.07.024"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ding, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Nohira, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hagiwara, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Fukunaga, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sakai, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Nitta, K.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electrochemical Performance of Hard Carbon Negative Electrodes for Ionic Liquid-Based Sodium Ion Batteries over a Wide Temperature Range</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Electrochim.                         cas_cit7R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">7</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrochemical performance of hard carbon negative electrodes for ionic liquid-based sodium ion batteries over a wide temperature range</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ding, Changsheng; Nohira, Toshiyuki; Hagiwara, Rika; Fukunaga, Atsushi; Sakai, Shoichiro; Nitta, Koji</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na ion batteries (SIBs) were attracting much attention as promising next-generation energy storage devices for large-scale applications.  The major safety issue with SIBs, which arises from the flammability and volatility of conventional org. solvent-based electrolytes, is resolved by adopting an ionic liq. (IL) electrolyte.  However, there are only a few reports on the study of neg. electrodes in ILs.  Here, the authors report the electrochem. performance of a hard C (Hc) neg. electrode in Na[FSA]-[C3C1pyrr][FSA] (FSA = bis(fluorosulfonyl)amide, C3C1pyrr = N-methyl-N-propylpyrrolidinium) IL over a wide temp. range of -10° to 90°.  High-temp. operation, which is realized for the 1st time by using an IL, can take full advantage of the high capacity of Hc even at a very high discharge rate of 1000 mA (g-Hc)-1: the discharge capacity is 230 mAh (g-Hc)-1 at 90° and 25 mAh (g-Hc)-1 at 25°.  Also, surprisingly stable cycleability is obsd. for the Hc electrode at 90°, i.e. a capacity retention ratio of 84% after 500 cycles.  Finally, a high full-cell voltage of 2.8 V and stable full-cell operation with Coulombic efficiency &gt;99% are achieved for the 1st time when using NaCrO2 as the pos. electrode at 90°.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoIpiXxMdBMKLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgwpvnezl0JEw"> &gt;&gt; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tao, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Facile Synthesis and Electrochemical Sodium Storage of CoS<sub>2</sub> Micro/Nano-Structures</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nano Res.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">9</span><span class="NLM_x"> (</span><span class="NLM_issue">1</span><span class="NLM_x">) </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">198</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">206</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit8R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">8</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Facile synthesis and electrochemical sodium storage of CoS2 micro/nano-structures</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Xue; Zhang, Kai; Lei, Kaixiang; Li, Fujun; Tao, Zhanliang; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Research</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">198-206</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NRAEB5</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1998-0000</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Springer GmbH</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">We report the synthesis and electrochem. sodium storage of cobalt disulfide (CoS2) with various micro/nano-structures.  CoS2 with microscale sizes are either assembled by nanoparticles (P-CoS2) via a facile solvothermal route or nanooctahedrons constructed solid (O-CoS2) and hollow microstructures (H-CoS2) fabricated by hydrothermal methods.  Among three morphologies, H-CoS2 exhibits the largest discharge capacities and best rate performance as anode of sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  Furthermore, H-CoS2 delivers a capacity of 690 mA·h·g-1 at 1 A·g-1 after 100 cycles in a potential range of 0.1-3.0 V, and ∼240 mA·h·g-1 over 800 cycles in the potential window of 1.0-3.0 V.  This cycling difference mainly lies in the two discharge plateaus obsd. in 0.1-3.0 V and one discharge plateau in 1.0-3.0 V.  To interpret the reactions, X-ray diffraction (XRD) and transmission electron microscopy (TEM) are applied.  The results show that at the first plateau around 1.4 V, the insertion reaction (CoS2 + xNa+ + xe- → NaxCoS2) occurs; while at the second plateau around 0.6 V, the conversion reaction (NaxCoS2 + (4 - x) Na+ + (4 - x)e- → Co + 2Na2S) takes place.  This provides insights for electrochem. sodium storage of CoS2 as the anode of SIBs.                         cas_cit9R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">9</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium Storage Behavior in Natural Graphite using Ether-based Electrolyte Systems</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Haegyeom; Hong, Jihyun; Park, Young-Uk; Kim, Jinsoo; Hwang, Insang; Kang, Kisuk</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">25</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">534-541</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">This work reports that natural graphite is capable of Na insertion and extn. with a remarkable reversibility using ether-based electrolytes.  Natural graphite (the most well-known anode material for Li-ion batteries) has been barely studied as a suitable anode for Na rechargeable batteries due to the lack of Na intercalation capability.  Herein, graphite is not only capable of Na intercalation but also exhibits outstanding performance as an anode for Na-ion batteries.  The graphite anode delivers a reversible capacity of ≈150 mA-h/g with a cycle stability for 2500 cycles, and more than 75 mA-h/g at 10 A/g despite its micrometer-size (≈100 μm).  An Na storage mechanism in graphite, where Na+-solvent co-intercalation occurs combined with partial pseudocapacitive behaviors, is shown.  It is demonstrated that the electrolyte solvent species significantly affect the electrochem. properties, not only rate capability but also redox potential.  The feasibility of graphite in a Na full cell is also confirmed in conjunction with the Na1.5VPO4.8F0.7 cathode, delivering an energy of ≈120 W-h/kg while maintaining ≈70% of the initial capacity after 250 cycles.  This exceptional behavior of natural graphite promises new avenues for the development of cost-effective and reliable Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpH2c5ZOoUcVbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgwpvnezl0JEw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhvFGiurrN&amp;md5=0bb4c36145b59a3b9727155eca307655</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref10"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref10'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">10</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit10" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2015.05.116"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cheng, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Niu, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Highly Stable and Ultrafast Electrode Reaction of Graphite for Sodium Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.                         cas_cit10R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">10</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Highly stable and ultrafast electrode reaction of graphite for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhu, Zhiqiang; Cheng, Fangyi; Hu, Zhe; Niu, Zhiqiang; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na ion battery is a potential sustainable energy storage system due to its abundance and low cost.  To date, some Na-storage anode materials have achieved long life span, but the rate performance still remains insufficient.  Herein, in some linear ether-based electrolytes, graphite can not only render unprecedented cyclability (∼6000 cycles), but also exhibit ultrahigh rate capability (up to 10 A g-1), along with a reversible capacity of ∼110 mAh g-1.  By combining electrochem. measurements and structural anal. (e.g. in situ Raman and ex situ XRD measurements), the authors reveal that graphite undergoes a stage-evolution mechanism induced by the insertion of solvated Na ions.  Also, kinetic studies showed that this process accompanies with an intercalation pseudocapacitive behavior, which should be responsible for the obtained superior electrode properties.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoU5_sCWs86ArVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgxiqucPcSCYQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXpt1egtrc%253D&amp;md5=1e95e26a885104d1798bb80e57bebb7f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref11"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref11'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">11</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit11" data-doi="10.1002/smll.201401521"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Luo, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gao, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Langrock, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mignerey, A.                         cas_cit11R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">11</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">An Advanced MoS2/Carbon Anode for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Jingjing; Luo, Chao; Gao, Tao; Langrock, Alex; Mignerey, Alice C.; Wang, Chunsheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">473-481</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SMALBC</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1613-6810</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">MoS2 is a promising anode for high-performance sodium-ion batteries due to high specific capacity, abundance, and low cost.  However, poor cycling stability, low rate capability and unclear electrochem. reaction mechanism are the main challenges for MoS2 anode in Na-ion batteries.  In this study, molybdenum disulfide/carbon (MoS2/C) nanospheres are fabricated and used for Na-ion battery anodes.  MoS2/C nanospheres deliver a reversible capacity of 520 mA-h/g at 0.1C and maintain capacity 400 mA-h/g for 300 cycles at a high c.d. of 1C, demonstrating the best cycling performance of MoS2 for Na-ion batteries to date.  The high capacity is attributed to the short ion and electron diffusion pathway, which enables fast charge transfer and low concn. polarization.  The stable cycling performance and high coulombic efficiency (∼100%) of MoS2/C nanospheres are ascribed to (a) highly reversible conversion reaction of MoS2 during sodiation/desodiation as evidenced by ex-situ x-ray diffraction and (b) the formation of a stable solid electrolyte interface layer in fluoroethylene carbonate based electrolyte as demonstrated by FTIR spectroscopy measurements.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqcL7gViWJlhrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgxiqucPcSCYQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtlOitbg%253D&amp;md5=6ec4e5e6db41f69f19d690e591e04ffa</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref12'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit12" data-doi="10.1002/advs.201500200"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kopold, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">van Aken, P. A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Maier, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yu, Y.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A General Strategy to Fabricate Carbon-Coated 3D Porous Interconnected Metal Sulfides: Case Study of SnS/C Nanocomposite for High-Performance Lithium and Sodium Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv.                         cas_cit12R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">12</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A General Strategy to Fabricate Carbon-Coated 3D Porous Interconnected Metal Sulfides: Case Study of SnS/C Nanocomposite for High-Performance Lithium and Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhu Changbao; Kopold Peter; van Aken Peter A; Maier Joachim; Li Weihan; Yu Yan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced science (Weinheim, Baden-Wurttemberg, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">2</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1500200</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2198-3844</span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">Transition metal sulfides have a great potential for energy storage due to the pronouncedly higher capacity (owing to conversion to metal or even alloy) than traditional insertion electrode materials.  However, the poor cycling stability still limits the development and application in lithium and sodium ion batteries.  Here, taking SnS as a model material, a novel general strategy is proposed to fabricate a 3D porous interconnected metal sulfide/carbon nanocomposite by the electrostatic spray deposition technique without adding any expensive carbonaceous materials such as graphene or carbon nanotube.  In this way, small nanorods of SnS are generated with sizes of ≈10-20 nm embedded in amorphous carbon and self-assembled into a 3D porous interconnected nanocomposite.  The SnS:C is directly deposited on the Ti foil as a current collector and neither conductive additives nor binder are needed for battery assembly.  Such electrodes exhibit a high reversible capacity, high rate capability, and long cycling stability for both lithium and sodium storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcSWKboLQvx6nxfKb6ELK8t0fW6udTcc2eaIMBaEWrJVE7ntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BC2svosVaiuw%253D%253D&amp;md5=3addf9153282a4b91c756413bb7d97a2</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref13'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit13" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201402428"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Choi, S.                         cas_cit13R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">13</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">3D MoS2-Graphene Microspheres Consisting of Multiple Nanospheres with Superior Sodium Ion Storage Properties</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Choi, Seung Ho; Ko, You Na; Lee, Jung-Kul; Kang, Yun Chan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">25</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1780-1788</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A novel anode material for sodium-ion batteries consisting of 3D graphene microspheres divided into several tens of uniform nanospheres coated with few-layered MoS2 by a one-pot spray pyrolysis process is prepd.  The first discharge/charge capacities of the composite microspheres are 797 and 573 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 0.2 A g-1.  The 600th discharge capacity of the composite microspheres at a c.d. of 1.5 A g-1 is 322 mA h g-1.  The Coulombic efficiency during the 600 cycles is as high as 99.98%.  The outstanding Na ion storage properties of the 3D MoS2-graphene composite microspheres may be attributed to the reduced stacking of the MoS2 layers and to the 3D structure of the porous graphene microspheres.  The reduced stacking of the MoS2 layers relaxes the strain and lowers the barrier for Na+ insertion.  The empty nanospheres of the graphene offer voids for vol. expansion and pathways for fast electron transfer during repeated cycling.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp5MXJGPkuEhLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgxiqucPcSCYQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXkvVSitbk%253D&amp;md5=18c752a0885c5236fc4aefe504f5d301</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref14'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit14" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2016.01.116"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qin, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yan, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Pan, L.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">ZnS Nanoparticles Embedded in Reduced Graphene Oxide as High Performance Anode Material of Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Electrochim.                         cas_cit14R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">14</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">ZnS nanoparticles embedded in reduced graphene oxide as high performance anode material of sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Qin, Wei; Li, Dongsheng; Zhang, Xiaojie; Yan, Dong; Hu, Bingwen; Pan, Likun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">ZnS nanoparticles embedded in reduced graphene oxide (RGO) were prepd. via a facile microwave-assisted method and applied as anode materials of Na-ion batteries (SIBs).  The as-prepd. composites exhibit excellent Na storage properties.  A max. specific capacity of 481 mAh g-1 at the specific current of 100 mA g-1 can be achieved after 50 cycles by optimizing the RGO content in the composites.  The improved Na-ion storage ability can be ascribed to the enhanced sp. surface area and increased elec. cond. due to the introduction of RGO and the decreased size of ZnS particles which can shorten the pathway of Na-ion diffusion and facilitate the reversible Na+ diffusion kinetics.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp7UTewmWD3R7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgxiqucPcSCYQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhtlWjurc%253D&amp;md5=28233b7b5d8a8c1539b4e4417aa9910d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref15'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit15" data-doi="10.1002/chem.201501759"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kang, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Shang, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jiao, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">WS<sub>2</sub> Nanowires as a High-Performance Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Chem. - Eur.                         cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">WS2 Nanowires as a High-Performance Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Yongchang; Zhang, Ning; Kang, Hongyan; Shang, Minghui; Jiao, Lifang; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry - A European Journal</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">21</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">33</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">11878-11884</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">We report the synthesis and anode application for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) of WS2 nanowires (WS2 NWs).  WS2 NWs with very thin diam. of ≈25 nm and expanded interlayer spacing of 0.83 nm were prepd. by using a facile solvothermal method followed by a heat treatment.  The as-prepd. WS2 NWs were evaluated as anode materials of SIBs in two potential windows of 0.01-2.5 V and 0.5-3 V.  WS2 NWs displayed a remarkable capacity (605.3 mA h/g at 100 mA/g) but with irreversible conversion reaction in the potential window of 0.01-2.5 V.  In comparison, WS2 NWs showed a reversible intercalation mechanism in the potential window of 0.5-3 V, in which the nanowire-framework is well maintained.  In the latter case, the interlayers of WS2 are gradually expanded and exfoliated during repeated charge-discharge cycling.  This not only provides more active sites and open channels for the intercalation of Na+ but also facilitates the electronic and ionic diffusion.  Therefore, WS2 NWs exhibited an ultra-long cycle life with high capacity and rate capability in the potential window of 0.5-3 V.  This study shows that WS2 NWs are promising as the anode materials of room-temp. SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqC-krHnyYYqrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgeCPIT6X0EWg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtFWgtb7F&amp;md5=2933590e4f46f62cc7a2a8a114b4935b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref16"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref16'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">16</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit16" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.6b00179"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Du, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xiong, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cui, G.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Nickel Disulfide-Graphene Nanosheets Composites with Improved Electrochemical Performance for Sodium Ion Battery</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Appl.                         cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Vanadium Sulfide on Reduced Graphene Oxide Layer as a Promising Anode for Sodium Ion Battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sun, Ruimin; Wei, Qiulong; Li, Qidong; Luo, Wen; An, Qinyou; Sheng, Jinzhi; Wang, Di; Chen, Wei; Mai, Liqiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">As an alternative system of rechargeable Li-ion batteries, Na-ion batteries revitalize researchers' interest due to the low cost, abundant Na resources, and similar storage mechanism to Li ion batteries.  VS4 has emerged as a promising anode material for SIBs due to low cost and its unique linear chains structure that can offer potential sites for Na storage.  Herein, the authors present the growth of VS4 on reduced graphene oxide (rGO) as SIBs anode for the 1st time.  The VS4/rGO anode exhibits promising performance in SIBs.  It delivers a reversible capacity of 362 mA h g-1 at 100 mA g-1 and a good rate performance.  The authors also study the Na storage behavior of the VS4/rGO.  Different than most transition metal sulfides, the VS4/rGO composite experiences a 3-step sepn. mechanism during the sodiation process (VS4 to metallic V and Na2S, then the electrochem. mechanism is akin to Na-S).  The VS4/rGO composite proves to be a promising material for rechargeable SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpiEKpa0_88WbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgeCPIT6X0EWg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsVeqsb3K&amp;md5=1bd6b7b28b6875016174fb475c0a70f3</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref18'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit18" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2016.01.092"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sun, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Rui, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jiang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sun, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Dou, S.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Bismuth Sulfide: a High-Capacity Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.                         cas_cit18R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">18</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Bismuth sulfide: A high-capacity anode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sun, Wenping; Rui, Xianhong; Zhang, Dan; Jiang, Yinzhu; Sun, Ziqi; Liu, Huakun; Dou, Shixue</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Exploring high-performance anode materials is currently one of the most urgent issues towards practical sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  In this work, Bi2S3 is demonstrated to be a high-capacity anode for SIBs for the first time.  The specific capacity of Bi2S3 nanorods achieves up to 658 and 264 mAh/g at a c.d. of 100 and 2000 mA/g, resp.  A full cell with Na3V2(PO4)3-based cathode is also assembled as a proof of concept and delivers 340 mAh/g at 100 mA/g.                         cas_cit19R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">19</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sensitive determination of caffeine by copper sulphide nanoparticles modified carbon paste electrode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Mahanthappa, Mallappa; Yellappa, Shivaraj; Kottam, Nagaraju; Srinivasa Rao Vusa, Chiranjeevi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Sensors and Actuators, A: Physical</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Copper sulfide nanoparticles (CuS NPs) were synthesized by simple co-pptn. method in aq. media using starch as a biopolymer.  The obtained product was characterized by XRD, SEM, EDX, TEM, FTIR and UV-vis techniques.  The particle size was detd. by TEM anal. and found to be in the range 20-50 nm.  CuS NPs modified carbon paste electrode (CuS NPs MCPE) was employed to det. caffeine (CAF) by cyclic voltammetry (CV) and differential pulse voltammetry (DPV) methods.  The CuS NPs MCPE showed better electrocatalytic activity towards the oxidn. of CAF, which was confirmed by enhance in the oxidn. peak current and decrease in oxidn. peak potential. Under exptl. conditions, the oxidn. current of CAF was proportional to its concn. from 2 μM to 120 μM.  The detection limit was found to be 18 × 10-9 M.                         cas_cit20R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">20</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A template-free facile approach for the synthesis of CuS-rGO nanocomposites towards enhanced photocatalytic reduction of organic contaminants and textile effluents</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Saranya, Murugan; Ramachandran, Rajendran; Kollu, Pratap; Jeong, Soon Kwan; Grace, Andrews Nirmala</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">RSC Advances</span>

The CuS-rGO nanocomposites was investigated using powder XRD, FE-SEM, HR-TEM, DRS UV-vis spectroscopy, photoluminescence (PL) measurements, infra-red spectroscopy and photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS). The photocatalytic properties of the composites were tested in a visible light photoreactor chamber.  The CuS-rGO nanocomposites were found to exhibit high photocatalytic activities with a max. efficiency of 99.27% after 60 min in a visible source.  These interesting and enhanced catalytic properties of CuS-rGO-x nanocomposite was further tested for org. contaminant and textile effluents collected from two different sites situated in the Thirupur textile industries, India.                         cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">One-Pot Synthesis of Copper Sulfide Nanowires/Reduced Graphene Oxide Nanocomposites with Excellent Lithium-Storage Properties as Anode Materials for Lithium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Feng, Caihong; Zhang, Le; Yang, Menghuan; Song, Xiangyun; Zhao, Hui; Jia, Zhe; Sun, Kening; Liu, Gao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">29</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">15726-15734</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Copper sulfide nanowires/reduced graphene oxide (CuSNWs/rGO) nanocomposites are successfully synthesized via a facile one-pot and template-free soln. method in a DMSO-Et glycol (EG) mixed solvent.  It is noteworthy that the precursor plays a crucial role in the formation of the nanocomposites structure.  SEM, TEM, XRD, IR and Raman spectroscopy are used to investigate the morphol. and structural evolution of CuSNWs/rGO nanocomposites.  The as-fabricated CuSNWs/rGO nanocomposites show remarkably improved Li-storage performance, excellent cycling stability as well as high-rate capability compared with pristine CuS nanowires.  It obtains a reversible capacity of 620 mA h g-1 at 0.5C (1C = 560 mA g-1) after 100 cycles and 320 mA h g-1 at a high current rate of 4C even after 430 cycles.  The excellent lithium storage performance is ascribed to the synergistic effect between CuS nanowires and rGO nanosheets.  The as-formed CuSNWs/rGO nanocomposites can effectively accommodate large vol. changes, supply a 2D conducting network and trap the polysulfides generated during the conversion reaction of CuS.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqc9xxvuKMDwLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhT-4AfVTtJ2w"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtFWgs7vO&amp;md5=44fa884c45dd5d732fcdafb1ba062d83</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit24" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2015.12.048"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Peng, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xi, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">He, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xia, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Okada, S.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Synthesis of Sub-10 nm Copper Sulphide Rods as High-Performance Anode for Long-Cycle Life Li-ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.                         cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Synthesis of sub-10 nm copper sulfide rods as high-performance anode for long-cycle life Li-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhou, Mingjiong; Peng, Na; Liu, Zhen; Xi, Yun; He, Huiqiu; Xia, Yonggao; Liu, Zhaoping; Okada, Shigeto</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Copper sulfide (CuS) nanorods with the size of sub-10 nm are synthesized via a facile sol-gel method without post-thermal treatment.  The as-prepd. CuS nanorods are characterized by X-ray diffraction, transmission electron microscope, and energy dispersive X-ray spectroscopy as hexagonal covellite CuS.  The as-prepd. CuS nanorods utilized as anode material exhibit a high reversible capacity and excellent cycling stability up to 250 cycles, as well as high Coulombic efficiency.         </div><div class="casAbstract">We study the synthesis and electrochem. and mech. performance of layered free-standing papers composed of acid-exfoliated few-layer molybdenum disulfide (MoS2) and reduced graphene oxide (rGO) flakes for use as a self-standing flexible electrode in sodium-ion batteries.  Synthesis was achieved through vacuum filtration of homogeneous dispersions consisting of varying wt. percent of acid-treated MoS2 flakes in GO in DI water, followed by thermal redn. at elevated temps.  The electrochem. performance of the crumpled composite paper (at 4 mg.cm-2) was evaluated as counter electrode against pure Na foil in a half-cell configuration.  The electrode showed good Na cycling ability with a stable charge capacity of ∼230 mAh.g-1 with respect to total wt. of the electrode with Coulombic efficiency reaching ∼99%.  In addn., static uniaxial tensile tests performed on crumpled composite papers showed high av. strain to failure reaching ∼2%.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqX-na1eCQtCLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhtNVXpQGs4bg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXpslejsw%253D%253D&amp;md5=d45da3902a48ed0a91ed1278d69862fb</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref27'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit27" data-doi="10.1039/c2cp44572g"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hariharan, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Saravanan, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ramar, V.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Balaya, P.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Rationally Designed Dual Role Anode Material for Lithium-Ion and Sodium-Ion Batteries: Case Study of Eco-Friendly Fe<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub></span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Phys.                         cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sb-C nanofibers with long cycle life as an anode material for high-performance sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wu, Lin; Hu, Xiaohong; Qian, Jiangfeng; Pei, Feng; Wu, Fayuan; Mao, Rongjun; Ai, Xinping; Yang, Hanxi; Cao, Yuliang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sb-C nanofibers are synthesized successfully through a single-nozzle electrospinning technique and subsequent calcination.  The structural and morphol. characterizations reveal the uniform nanofiber structure with the Sb nanoparticles embedded homogeneously in the carbon nanofibers.  Electrochem. expts. show that the Sb-C nanofiber electrode can deliver large reversible capacity (631 mA h g-1) at C/15, greatly improved rate capability (337 mA h g-1 at 5 C) and excellent cycling stability (90% capacity retention after 400 cycles).  The superior electrochem. performances of the Sb-C nanofibers are due to the unique nanofiber structure and uniform distribution of Sb nanoparticles in carbon matrix, which provides a conductive and buffering matrix for effective release of mech. stress caused by Na ion insertion/extn. and prevent the aggregation of the Sb nanoparticles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqODsgQsiGAJrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj-7b8avxqgaw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhvFKhtrrN&amp;md5=b043a6265ebe5b5183098fbd4c98cc1f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref29'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit29" data-doi="10.1039/c4ta01324g"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Nithya, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gopukumar, S.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">RGO/nano Sb Composite: a High Performance Anode Material for Na<sup>+</sup> Ion Batteries and Evidence for the Formation of Nanoribbons from the Nano rGO Sheet during Galvanostatic Cycling</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.                         cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">rGO/nano Sb composite: a high performance anode material for Na+ ion batteries and evidence for the formation of nanoribbons from the nano rGO sheet during galvanostatic cycling</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Nithya, C.; Gopukumar, S.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">2</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">27</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">10516-10525</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Lithium ion batteries exhibit high energy and power densities, thereby making them a promising power sources for multifarious applications.  However, the abundance of lithium (Li) is one of the major crit. issues for using Li battery technologies.  Therefore, for large-scale applications a sodium (Na) ion battery is one of the apt alternatives for portable electronics instead of expensive Li ion batteries.  One of the challenging issues in Na+ ion batteries is the difficulty to understand the chem. involved in view of the large size of the Na+ ion as compared to the Li+ ion, which makes the alloying/dealloying difficult during cycling.  Hence, in this present work, we explore an innovative concept of storing Na+ ions in reduced graphene oxide/antimony (Sb) metal composites.  Such a concept of storing Na+ in the rGO/Sb composite is one of the simplest ways to enhance the electrochem. performance of metal-based anodes for sodium ion batteries.  Furthermore, it is seen that the nano rGO sheet transforms to nanoribbons upon galvanostatic cycling, as evidenced by TEM.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGryp-lzHn0P9rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj-7b8avxqgaw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhtVWrtbbF&amp;md5=0cb4120ef4c51ee603ae519957bf98c0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref30'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit30" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2015.01.092"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, Z.-J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, Y.-X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chou, S.-L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, H.-J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, H.-K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, J.-Z.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Rapid Synthesis of α-Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO Nanocomposites by Microwave Autoclave as Superior Anodes for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.         (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">VO2 (B) is an interesting cathode candidate in lithium-ion batteries with a high theor. capacity and fast charge/mass transfer rate.  Most of the studies on this material have focused on the lithium insertion reaction in the range of 4.0-1.0 V.  In this paper, VO2/rGO nanocomposite was prepd. by a microwave-assisted solvothermal method and investigated in both lithium-ion and sodium-ion batteries as a potential anode.  The VO2 (B) nanorods have an av. diam. of ∼200 nm, and is encapsulated by reduced graphene oxide (rGO) nanosheets.  Electrochem. results reveal that the VO2/rGO electrodes exhibit stable cycling and good rate performance in both Li and Na cells.  Reversible capacities of 400 mA h g-1 over 400 cycles (vs. Li/Li+) and 200 mA h g-1 over 200 cycles (vs. Na/Na+) have been achieved, indicating it is potential as an anode candidate either in lithium- or sodium-ion batteries.  Nevertheless, the reaction mechanisms seem to be different in Li and Na cells.  The crystal structure of VO2 (B) is maintained at a low discharge potential of 0.05 V in lithium-ion cells, while phase amorphization occurs in sodium-ion cells below 0.5 V.  This result is consistent with the previous study on TiO2, further confirming that some stable metal oxides may show rather different behaviors in Na cells than expected.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo5rtd1GvwU2bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lihcsBtBJtWjw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtFSksrzL&amp;md5=58cecc88180fdde5de03e7ad9905bed0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref35"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref35'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">35</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit35" data-doi="10.1039/C3CC47977C"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jian, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhao, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zheng, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Shi, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, H.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> Nanocrystals Anchored onto Graphene Nanosheets as the Anode Material for Low-Cost Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Chem.                         cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Slater, Michael D.; Kim, Donghan; Lee, Eungje; Doeff, Marca; Johnson, Christopher S.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">23</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The status of ambient temp. sodium ion batteries is reviewed in light of recent developments in anode, electrolyte and cathode materials.  These devices, although early in their stage of development, are promising for large-scale grid storage applications due to the abundance and very low cost of sodium-contg. precursors used to make the components.  The engineering knowledge developed recently for highly successful Li ion batteries can be leveraged to ensure rapid progress in this area, although different electrode materials and electrolytes will be required for dual intercalation systems based on sodium.  In particular, new anode materials need to be identified, since the graphite anode, commonly used in lithium systems, does not intercalate sodium to any appreciable extent.  A wider array of choices is available for cathodes, including high performance layered transition metal oxides and polyanionic compds.  Recent developments in electrodes are encouraging, but a great deal of research is necessary, particularly in new electrolytes, and the understanding of the SEI films.  The engineering modeling calcns. of Na-ion battery energy d. indicate that 210 Wh kg-1 in gravimetric energy is possible for Na-ion batteries compared to existing Li-ion technol. if a cathode capacity of 200 mAh g-1 and a 500 mAh g-1 anode can be discovered with an av. cell potential of 3.3 V.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGojsFXLPEQzILVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj6jItitKcvVg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XntlSnurc%253D&amp;md5=fa5d7d089d261a40896cb6b03e88bfbe</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref37"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref37'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">37</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit37" data-doi="10.1039/C4EE03759F"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cheng, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Pyrite FeS<sub>2</sub> for High-Rate and Long-Life Rechargeable Sodium Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Energy Environ.                         cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Pyrite FeS2 for high-rate and long-life rechargeable sodium batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hu, Zhe; Zhu, Zhiqiang; Cheng, Fangyi; Zhang, Kai; Wang, Jianbin; Chen, Chengcheng; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1309-1316</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1754-5706</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">It is desirable to develop electrode materials for advanced rechargeable batteries with low cost, long life, and high-rate capability.  Pyrite FeS2, as an easily obtained natural mineral, has been already commercialized in primary lithium batteries, but encountered problems in rechargeable batteries with carbonate-based electrolytes due to the limited cycle life caused by the conversion-type reaction (FeS2 + 4M → Fe + 2M2S (M = Li or Na)).  Herein, we demonstrate that FeS2 microspheres can be applied in room-temp. rechargeable sodium batteries with only the intercalation reaction by simultaneously selecting a compatible NaSO3CF3/diglyme electrolyte and tuning the cut-off voltage to 0.8 V.  A surprisingly high-rate capability (170 mA h g-1 at 20 A g-1) and unprecedented long-term cyclability (∼90% capacity retention for 20 000 cycles) has been obtained.  We suggest that a stable elec. conductive layer-structured NaxFeS2 was formed during cycling, which enables the highly reversible sodium intercalation and deintercalation.  Moreover, 18650-type sodium batteries were constructed exhibiting a high capacity of ∼4200 mA h (corresponding to 126 W h kg-1 and 382 W h L-1) and a capacity retention of 97% after an initial 200 cycles at 4 A during charge-discharge.  This shows that the prodn. of rechargeable sodium batteries with FeS2 microspheres is viable for com. utilization.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrFxqeM-EGKh7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj6jItitKcvVg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhs1arsL0%253D&amp;md5=25c3d019d88687effcc5109727ee9bce</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref38'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit38" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201501785"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Su, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kretschmer, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, G.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Improved Electrochemical Performance of Na-Ion Batteries in Ether-Based Electrolytes: A Case Study of ZnS Nanospheres</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The use is demonstrated of FeSe2 as an anode material for sodium-ion batteries.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Exploitation of high-performance anode materials is essential but challenging to the development of sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  Among all proposed anode materials for SIBs, sulfides were proved promising candidates due to their unique chem. and phys. properties.  A facile solvothermal method to in situ decorate cobalt sulfide (CoS) nanoplates on reduced graphene oxide (rGO) to build CoS@rGO composite is described.  When evaluated as anode for SIBs, an impressive high specific capacity (540 mAh/g at 1 A/g), excellent rate capability (636 mAh/g at 0.1 A/g and 306 mAh/g at 10 A/g), and extraordinarily cycle stability (420 mAh/g at 1 A/g after 1000 cycles) were demonstrated by CoS@rGO composite for sodium storage.  The synergetic effect between the CoS nanoplates and rGO matrix contributes to the enhanced electrochem. performance of the hybrid composite.  The results provide a facile approach to fabricate promising anode materials for high-performance SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGotD1r43G7-ibVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lifxFdsFHSZ_g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xns1Cjtw%253D%253D&amp;md5=7834a86a1d3c3333ee7594239160e829</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref44"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref44'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">44</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit44" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2015.05.055"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qin, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sun, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Pan, L.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">GeO<sub>2</sub> Decorated Reduced Graphene Oxide as Anode Material of Sodium Ion Battery</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Electrochim.                         cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">GeO2 decorated reduced graphene oxide as anode material of sodium ion battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Qin, Wei; Chen, Taiqiang; Hu, Bingwen; Sun, Zhuo; Pan, Likun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">GeO2-reduced graphene oxide (RGO) composites were prepd. by a simple freeze-drying method.  After thermal annealing in N2 atmosphere at 450° for 2 h, the composites were examd. as anode materials of Na ion batteries for the 1st time.  Their morphol., structure and electrochem. performance were characterized by field-emission SEM, x-ray diffraction, N2 adsorption-desorption isotherm, cyclic voltammetry and electrochem. impedance spectroscopy, resp.  A max. specific capacity of 330 mAh g-1 can be achieved after 50 galvanostatic charge-discharge cycles at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1 by tuning the RGO content in the composites.
