                        cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Porous CuO nanowires as the anode of rechargeable Na-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Lijiang; Zhang, Kai; Hu, Zhe; Duan, Wenchao; Cheng, Fangyi; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Research</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">199-208</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NRAEB5</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1998-0000</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Springer GmbH</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">We report the prepn. of porous CuO nanowires that are composed of nanoparticles (∼50 nm) via a simple decompn. of a Cu(OH)2 precursor and their application as the anode materials of rechargeable Na-ion batteries.  The as-prepd. porous CuO nanowires exhibit a Brunauer-Emmett-Teller (BET) surface area of 13.05 m2·g-1, which is six times larger than that of bulk CuO (2.16 m2·g-1).  The anode of porous CuO nanowires showed discharge capacities of 640 mA·h·g-1 in the first cycle and 303 mA·h·g-1 after 50 cycles at 50 mA·g-1.  The high capacity is attributed to porous nanostructure which facilitates fast Na-intercalation kinetics.  The mechanism of electrochem. Na-storage based on conversion reactions has been studied through cyclic voltammetry, X-ray diffraction (XRD), Raman spectroscopy, and high resoln. transmission electron microscopy (HRTEM).  It is demonstrated that in the discharge process, Na+ ions first insert into CuO to form a Cu1-xIICuxIO1-x/2 solid and a Na2O matrix then Cu1-xIICuxIO1-x/2 reacts with Na+ to produce Cu2O, and finally Cu2O decomp. into Cu nanoparticles enclosed in a Na2O matrix.  During the charge process, Cu nanoparticles are first oxidized to generate Cu2O and then converted back to CuO.  This result contributes to the design and mechanistic anal. of high-performance anodes for rechargeable Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrxvWXcK-rpArVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhBXB25fMX5pQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhvFyltbbO&amp;md5=07cf7e146303cae03a93a1846b17d7bd</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref46'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit46" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2016.04.042"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yuan, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Huang, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yin, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, L.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Facile Synthesis of CuS/rGO Composite with Enhanced Electrochemical Lithium-Storage Properties through Microwave-Assisted Hydrothermal Method</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Electrochim. Acta</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">203</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">238</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">245</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.electacta.2016.04.042</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D203%26publication_year%3D2016%26pages%3D238-245%26journal%3DElectrochim.%2BActa%26author%3DD.%2BYuan%26author%3DG.%2BHuang%26author%3DF.%2BZhang%26author%3DD.%2BYin%26author%3DL.%2BWang%26title%3DFacile%2BSynthesis%2Bof%2BCuS%252FrGO%2BComposite%2Bwith%2BEnhanced%2BElectrochemical%2BLithium-Storage%2BProperties%2Bthrough%2BMicrowave-Assisted%2BHydrothermal%2BMethod%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.electacta.2016.04.042&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.6b12529&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.electacta.2016.04.042&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit46R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">46</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Facile synthesis of CuS/rGO composite with enhanced electrochemical lithium-storage properties through microwave-assisted hydrothermal method</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yuan, Dongxia; Huang, Gang; Zhang, Feifei; Yin, Dongming; Wang, Limin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">203</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">238-245</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ELCAAV</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4686</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Cu sulfide nanoflower/reduced graphene oxide (CuS/rGO) composite was synthesized using Cu(NO3)2, thiourea (Tu) and graphene oxide (GO) powers as the precursor by an ultrafast microwave-assisted hydrothermal method.  The electrochem. performances of CuS/rGO composite as anode material of Li ion batteries (LIBs) were studied both in ether-based (LiTFSI in DOL/DME) and carbonate-based electrolytes (LiPF6 in EC/DMC).  CuS/rGO composite exhibits excellent electrochem. Li-storage properties.  The reversible capacity of 422 mA h g-1 and 390 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1 after 70 cycles was obtained in both electrolytes, resp.  Even after 200 charge-discharge cycles at 500 mA g-1 in ether-based electrolyte, the composite delivers a good discharge capacity of 390 mA h g-1 with high capacity retention ratio of 96.7%.  The good electrochem. performances of CuS/rGO can be attributed to the synergistic effect of the CuS nanoflower and rGO.  Briefly, the introduction of rGO can improve the electronic cond. of the composite, effectively immobilize the CuS and inhibit the dissoln. of the polysulfide intermediates generated during the charge-discharge process.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqMymmXOZ2BKbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhBXB25fMX5pQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XmtFeksb8%253D&amp;md5=ef777b29f430f7ddde86f541c0098d9e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref47"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref47'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">47</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit47" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201403734"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jache, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Adelhelm, P.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Use of Graphite as a Highly Reversible Electrode with Superior Cycle Life for Sodium-Ion Batteries by Making Use of Co-Intercalation Phenomena</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">53</span><span class="NLM_x"> (</span><span class="NLM_issue">38</span><span class="NLM_x">) </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">10169</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">10173</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/anie.201403734</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D53%26publication_year%3D2014%26pages%3D10169-10173%26journal%3DAngew.%2BChem.%252C%2BInt.%2BEd.%26issue%3D38%26author%3DB.%2BJache%26author%3DP.%2BAdelhelm%26title%3DUse%2Bof%2BGraphite%2Bas%2Ba%2BHighly%2BReversible%2BElectrode%2Bwith%2BSuperior%2BCycle%2BLife%2Bfor%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%2Bby%2BMaking%2BUse%2Bof%2BCo-Intercalation%2BPhenomena%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fanie.201403734&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.6b12529&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fanie.201403734&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit47R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">47</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Use of Graphite as a Highly Reversible Electrode with Superior Cycle Life for Sodium-Ion Batteries by Making Use of Co-Intercalation Phenomena</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jache, Birte; Adelhelm, Philipp</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">53</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">38</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">10169-10173</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ACIEF5</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1433-7851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Although being the std. anode material in Li-ion batteries (LIBs), graphite so far is considered to fail application in Na-ion batteries (NIBs) because the Na-C system lacks suitable binary intercalation compds.  This limitation can be circumvented by using co-intercalation phenomena in a diglyme-based electrolyte.  The resulting compd. is a stage-I ternary intercalation compd. with an estd. stoichiometry of Na(diglyme)2C20.  Highlights of the electrode reaction are its high energy efficiency, the small irreversible loss during the 1st cycle, and a superior cycle life with capacities close to 100 mA-h g-1 for 1000 cycles and coulomb efficiencies &gt;99.87%.  A 1-to-one comparison with the analog Li-based cell shows that the Na-based system performs better and also withstands higher currents.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrIP5gn46fMJLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhBXB25fMX5pQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXht1WlsbbE&amp;md5=80e4b709236b714939a54f259d959661</span></div></div></div></div></li></ol></div><script type="text/javascript" nonce="90f6e7e75ed6775c-LHR">window.refViewer={'ref1':['cit1'],'ref2':['cit2'],'ref3':['cit3'],'ref4':['cit4'],'ref5':['cit5'],'ref6':['cit6'],'ref7':['cit7'],'ref8':['cit8'],'ref9':['cit9'],'ref10':['cit10'],'ref11':['cit11'],'ref12':['cit12'],'ref13':['cit13'],'ref14':['cit14'],'ref15':['cit15'],'ref16':['cit16'],'ref17':['cit17'],'ref18':['cit18'],'ref19':['cit19'],'ref20':['cit20'],'ref21':['cit21'],'ref22':['cit22'],'ref23':['cit23'],'ref24':['cit24'],'ref25':['cit25'],'ref26':['cit26'],'ref27':['cit27'],'ref28':['cit28'],'ref29':['cit29'],'ref30':['cit30'],'ref31':['cit31'],'ref32':['cit32'],'ref33':['cit33'],'ref34':['cit34'],'ref35':['cit35'],'ref36':['cit36'],'ref37':['cit37'],'ref38':['cit38'],'ref39':['cit39'],'ref40':['cit40'],'ref41':['cit41'],'ref42':['cit42'],'ref43':['cit43'],'ref44':['cit44'],'ref45':['cit45'],'ref46':['cit46'],'ref47':['cit47']}</script><div class="articleCitedByDropzone" data-pb-dropzone="articleCitedByDropzone"><div class="cited-by"><div class="article_content-header cited-content_header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div tabindex="0" class="article_content-title"><h2 id="citeThis">Cited By</h2><div class="article__copy"> <button class="article__copy__btn"><i aria-hidden="true" class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><div class="cited-by__content"><div class="sciteMetricsDropzone">

                        rightTab-cas_cit1R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">1</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrode materials for rechargeable sodium-ion batteries: potential alternatives to current lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Sung-Wook; Seo, Dong-Hwa; Ma, Xiaohua; Ceder, Gerbrand; Kang, Kisuk</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2012</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">2</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Lithium (Li)-ion batteries (LIB) have governed the current worldwide rechargeable battery market due to their outstanding energy and power capability.  In particular, the LIB's role in enabling elec. vehicles (EVs) has been highlighted to replace the current oil-driven vehicles in order to reduce the usage of oil resources and generation of CO2 gases.  Unlike Li, sodium is one of the more abundant elements on Earth and exhibits similar chem. properties to Li, indicating that Na chem. could be applied to a similar battery system.  In the 1970s-80s, both Na-ion and Li-ion electrodes were investigated, but the higher energy d. of Li-ion cells made them more applicable to small, portable electronic devices, and research efforts for rechargeable batteries have been mainly concd. on LIB since then.  Recently, research interest in Na-ion batteries (NIB) has been resurrected, driven by new applications with requirements different from those in portable electronics, and to address the concern on Li abundance.  In this article, both neg. and pos. electrode materials in NIB are briefly reviewed.  While the voltage is generally lower and the vol. change upon Na removal or insertion is larger for Na-intercalation electrodes, compared to their Li equiv., the power capability can vary depending on the crystal structures.  It is concluded that cost-effective NIB can partially replace LIB, but requires further investigation and improvement.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGonnrfiSUpaRrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljMRIcZAzBWOA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XhtVOrtLjF&amp;md5=485b20393bb8876b2f69ca708aeba606</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref2" class="rightTabRefNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit2" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201410376"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kundu, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Talaie, E.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Duffort, V.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Nazar, L.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Layered transition metal oxides are considered promising cathodes for sodium ion batteries (SIBs) due to their superior specific capacities.  However, they usually suffer from insufficient cycling and rate performance mainly from the structural instability during repeated cycles.  These longstanding challenges are overcome by engaging crystal water in the interlayer space of sodium manganese oxide under the Birnessite framework.  The crystal water enhances Na ion diffusion both in the crystal host and at the interface, suppresses fatal Mn2+ dissoln., and improves long-term structural stability, leading to excellent performance in rate capability and cycle life.  The current study suggests that many hydrated materials can be good candidates for electrode materials of emerging rechargeable batteries that need to deal with the large size or multivalent charge of their carrier ions.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGorAuRErefm87Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgJaJI5MT6hlA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXnvFClsrw%253D&amp;md5=c97f9664dda9f15a0a6d53fd9366b614</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref4" class="rightTabRefNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit4" data-doi="10.1021/acs.jpclett.5b00868"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Dall’Agnese, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Taberna, P.-L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gogotsi, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Simon, P.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Two-Dimensional Vanadium Carbide (MXene) as Positive Electrode for Sodium-Ion Capacitors</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J. Phys. Chem.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Ion capacitors store energy through intercalation of cations into an electrode at a faster rate than in batteries and within a larger potential window.  These devices reach a higher energy d. compared to electrochem. double layer capacitor.  Li-ion capacitors are already produced com., but the development of Na-ion capacitors is hindered by lack of materials that would allow fast intercalation of Na-ions.  Here the electrochem. behavior is investigated of 2D vanadium carbide, V2C, from the MXene family.  We investigated the mechanism is investigated of Na intercalation by XRD and achieved capacitance of ∼100 F/g at 0.2 mV/s.  A full cell is assembled with hard carbon as neg. electrode, a known anode material for Na ion batteries, and achieved capacity of 50 mAh/g with a max. cell voltage of 3.5 V.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq2xPLi_Be8qrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgJaJI5MT6hlA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXps1akuro%253D&amp;md5=8023bd6346d6b8aaf4d36a47a5163d1c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref5" class="rightTabRefNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit5" data-doi="10.1038/srep09254"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xiong, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Luo, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qie, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hou, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Huang, Y.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Flexible Membranes of MoS<sub>2</sub>/C Nanofibers by Electrospinning as Binder-Free Anodes for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Sci.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A flexible membrane consisting of MoS2/carbon nanofibers has been fabricated by a simple electrospinning method.  MoS2 nanosheets are uniformly encapsulated in the inter-connected carbon nanofibers with diams. of ∼150 nm.  When evaluated as a binder-free electrode for sodium-ion batteries, the as-obtained electrode demonstrates high performances, including high reversible capacity of 381.7 mA h g-1 at 100 mA g-1 and superior rate capability (283.3, 246.5 and 186.3 mA h g-1 at 0.5, 1 and 2 A g-1, resp.).                         rightTab-cas_cit6R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">6</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High cyclability of carbon-coated TiO2 nanoparticles as anode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ge, Yeqian; Jiang, Han; Zhu, Jiadeng; Lu, Yao; Chen, Chen; Hu, Yi; Qiu, Yiping; Zhang, Xiangwu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Owing to the merits of good chem. stability, elemental abundance and nontoxicity, TiO2 (TiO2) has drawn increasing attraction for use as anode material in Na-ion batteries.  Nanostructured TiO2 was able to achieve high energy d.  However, nanosized TiO2 is typically electrochem. instable, which leads to poor cycling performance.  To improve the cycling stability, C from thermolysis of poly(vinyl pyrrolidone) was coated onto TiO2 nanoparticles.  Electronic cond. and electrochem. stability were enhanced by coating C onto TiO2 nanoparticles.  The resultant C-coated TiO2 nanoparticles exhibited high reversible capacity (242.3 mAh g-1), high coulombic efficiency (97.8%), and good capacity retention (87.0%) at 30 mA g-1 over 100 cycles.  By comparison, untreated TiO2 nanoparticles showed comparable reversible capacity (237.3 mAh g-1) and coulombic efficiency (96.2%), but poor capacity retention (53.2%) under the same condition.  The rate performance of C-coated TiO2 nanoparticles was also displayed ≤127.6 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 800 mA g-1.  The improved cycling performance and rate capability were mostly attributed to protective C layer helping stabilize solid electrolyte interface formation of TiO2 nanoparticles and improving the electronic cond.  Therefore, C-coated TiO2 nanoparticles are promising anode candidate for Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqcVSv_A0qWyrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgJaJI5MT6hlA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtlOnurg%253D&amp;md5=845e991863dbb9108adc17af6da9f7f0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref7"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref7" class="rightTabRefNumLink">7</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit7" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2015.07.024"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ding, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Nohira, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hagiwara, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Fukunaga, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sakai, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Nitta, K.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electrochemical Performance of Hard Carbon Negative Electrodes for Ionic Liquid-Based Sodium Ion Batteries over a Wide Temperature Range</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Electrochim.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Na ion batteries (SIBs) were attracting much attention as promising next-generation energy storage devices for large-scale applications.  The major safety issue with SIBs, which arises from the flammability and volatility of conventional org. solvent-based electrolytes, is resolved by adopting an ionic liq. (IL) electrolyte.  However, there are only a few reports on the study of neg. electrodes in ILs.  Here, the authors report the electrochem. performance of a hard C (Hc) neg. electrode in Na[FSA]-[C3C1pyrr][FSA] (FSA = bis(fluorosulfonyl)amide, C3C1pyrr = N-methyl-N-propylpyrrolidinium) IL over a wide temp. range of -10° to 90°.  High-temp. operation, which is realized for the 1st time by using an IL, can take full advantage of the high capacity of Hc even at a very high discharge rate of 1000 mA (g-Hc)-1: the discharge capacity is 230 mAh (g-Hc)-1 at 90° and 25 mAh (g-Hc)-1 at 25°.  Also, surprisingly stable cycleability is obsd. for the Hc electrode at 90°, i.e. a capacity retention ratio of 84% after 500 cycles.         </div><div class="casAbstract">We report the synthesis and electrochem. sodium storage of cobalt disulfide (CoS2) with various micro/nano-structures.  CoS2 with microscale sizes are either assembled by nanoparticles (P-CoS2) via a facile solvothermal route or nanooctahedrons constructed solid (O-CoS2) and hollow microstructures (H-CoS2) fabricated by hydrothermal methods.  Among three morphologies, H-CoS2 exhibits the largest discharge capacities and best rate performance as anode of sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  Furthermore, H-CoS2 delivers a capacity of 690 mA·h·g-1 at 1 A·g-1 after 100 cycles in a potential range of 0.1-3.0 V, and ∼240 mA·h·g-1 over 800 cycles in the potential window of 1.0-3.0 V.  This cycling difference mainly lies in the two discharge plateaus obsd. in 0.1-3.0 V and one discharge plateau in 1.0-3.0 V.  To interpret the reactions, X-ray diffraction (XRD) and transmission electron microscopy (TEM) are applied.  The results show that at the first plateau around 1.4 V, the insertion reaction (CoS2 + xNa+ + xe- → NaxCoS2) occurs; while at the second plateau around 0.6 V, the conversion reaction (NaxCoS2 + (4 - x) Na+ + (4 - x)e- → Co + 2Na2S) takes place.  This provides insights for electrochem. sodium storage of CoS2 as the anode of SIBs.         </div><div class="casAbstract">This work reports that natural graphite is capable of Na insertion and extn. with a remarkable reversibility using ether-based electrolytes.  Natural graphite (the most well-known anode material for Li-ion batteries) has been barely studied as a suitable anode for Na rechargeable batteries due to the lack of Na intercalation capability.  Herein, graphite is not only capable of Na intercalation but also exhibits outstanding performance as an anode for Na-ion batteries.  The graphite anode delivers a reversible capacity of ≈150 mA-h/g with a cycle stability for 2500 cycles, and more than 75 mA-h/g at 10 A/g despite its micrometer-size (≈100 μm).  An Na storage mechanism in graphite, where Na+-solvent co-intercalation occurs combined with partial pseudocapacitive behaviors, is shown.  It is demonstrated that the electrolyte solvent species significantly affect the electrochem. properties, not only rate capability but also redox potential.  The feasibility of graphite in a Na full cell is also confirmed in conjunction with the Na1.5VPO4.8F0.7 cathode, delivering an energy of ≈120 W-h/kg while maintaining ≈70% of the initial capacity after 250 cycles.  This exceptional behavior of natural graphite promises new avenues for the development of cost-effective and reliable Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpH2c5ZOoUcVbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljg4i_Rkx6f5A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhvFGiurrN&amp;md5=0bb4c36145b59a3b9727155eca307655</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref10"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref10" class="rightTabRefNumLink">10</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit10" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2015.05.116"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cheng, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Niu, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Highly Stable and Ultrafast Electrode Reaction of Graphite for Sodium Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.                         rightTab-cas_cit11R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">11</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">An Advanced MoS2/Carbon Anode for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Jingjing; Luo, Chao; Gao, Tao; Langrock, Alex; Mignerey, Alice C.; Wang, Chunsheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">473-481</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SMALBC</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">MoS2 is a promising anode for high-performance sodium-ion batteries due to high specific capacity, abundance, and low cost.  However, poor cycling stability, low rate capability and unclear electrochem. reaction mechanism are the main challenges for MoS2 anode in Na-ion batteries.  In this study, molybdenum disulfide/carbon (MoS2/C) nanospheres are fabricated and used for Na-ion battery anodes.  MoS2/C nanospheres deliver a reversible capacity of 520 mA-h/g at 0.1C and maintain capacity 400 mA-h/g for 300 cycles at a high c.d. of 1C, demonstrating the best cycling performance of MoS2 for Na-ion batteries to date.  The high capacity is attributed to the short ion and electron diffusion pathway, which enables fast charge transfer and low concn. polarization.  The stable cycling performance and high coulombic efficiency (∼100%) of MoS2/C nanospheres are ascribed to (a) highly reversible conversion reaction of MoS2 during sodiation/desodiation as evidenced by ex-situ x-ray diffraction and (b) the formation of a stable solid electrolyte interface layer in fluoroethylene carbonate based electrolyte as demonstrated by FTIR spectroscopy measurements.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqcL7gViWJlhrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljg4i_Rkx6f5A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtlOitbg%253D&amp;md5=6ec4e5e6db41f69f19d690e591e04ffa</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref12" class="rightTabRefNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit12" data-doi="10.1002/advs.201500200"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kopold, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">van Aken, P.                         rightTab-cas_cit12R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">12</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A General Strategy to Fabricate Carbon-Coated 3D Porous Interconnected Metal Sulfides: Case Study of SnS/C Nanocomposite for High-Performance Lithium and Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhu Changbao; Kopold Peter; van Aken Peter A; Maier Joachim; Li Weihan; Yu Yan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced science (Weinheim, Baden-Wurttemberg, Germany)</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">2</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1500200</span>

    </div><div class="casAbstract">Transition metal sulfides have a great potential for energy storage due to the pronouncedly higher capacity (owing to conversion to metal or even alloy) than traditional insertion electrode materials.  However, the poor cycling stability still limits the development and application in lithium and sodium ion batteries.  Here, taking SnS as a model material, a novel general strategy is proposed to fabricate a 3D porous interconnected metal sulfide/carbon nanocomposite by the electrostatic spray deposition technique without adding any expensive carbonaceous materials such as graphene or carbon nanotube.  In this way, small nanorods of SnS are generated with sizes of ≈10-20 nm embedded in amorphous carbon and self-assembled into a 3D porous interconnected nanocomposite.  The SnS:C is directly deposited on the Ti foil as a current collector and neither conductive additives nor binder are needed for battery assembly.  Such electrodes exhibit a high reversible capacity, high rate capability, and long cycling stability for both lithium and sodium storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcSWKboLQvx6nxfKb6ELK8t0fW6udTcc2eZvZCdhoZxW5Lntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BC2svosVaiuw%253D%253D&amp;md5=3addf9153282a4b91c756413bb7d97a2</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref13" class="rightTabRefNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit13" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201402428"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Choi, S.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A novel anode material for sodium-ion batteries consisting of 3D graphene microspheres divided into several tens of uniform nanospheres coated with few-layered MoS2 by a one-pot spray pyrolysis process is prepd.  The first discharge/charge capacities of the composite microspheres are 797 and 573 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 0.2 A g-1.  The 600th discharge capacity of the composite microspheres at a c.d. of 1.5 A g-1 is 322 mA h g-1.  The Coulombic efficiency during the 600 cycles is as high as 99.98%.  The outstanding Na ion storage properties of the 3D MoS2-graphene composite microspheres may be attributed to the reduced stacking of the MoS2 layers and to the 3D structure of the porous graphene microspheres.  The reduced stacking of the MoS2 layers relaxes the strain and lowers the barrier for Na+ insertion.  The empty nanospheres of the graphene offer voids for vol. expansion and pathways for fast electron transfer during repeated cycling.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp5MXJGPkuEhLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljg4i_Rkx6f5A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXkvVSitbk%253D&amp;md5=18c752a0885c5236fc4aefe504f5d301</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref14" class="rightTabRefNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit14" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2016.01.116"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qin, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yan, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Pan, L.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">ZnS Nanoparticles Embedded in Reduced Graphene Oxide as High Performance Anode Material of Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Electrochim.         </div><div class="casAbstract">ZnS nanoparticles embedded in reduced graphene oxide (RGO) were prepd. via a facile microwave-assisted method and applied as anode materials of Na-ion batteries (SIBs).  The as-prepd. composites exhibit excellent Na storage properties.         </div><div class="casAbstract">We report the synthesis and anode application for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) of WS2 nanowires (WS2 NWs).  WS2 NWs with very thin diam. of ≈25 nm and expanded interlayer spacing of 0.83 nm were prepd. by using a facile solvothermal method followed by a heat treatment.  The as-prepd. WS2 NWs were evaluated as anode materials of SIBs in two potential windows of 0.01-2.5 V and 0.5-3 V.  WS2 NWs displayed a remarkable capacity (605.3 mA h/g at 100 mA/g) but with irreversible conversion reaction in the potential window of 0.01-2.5 V.  In comparison, WS2 NWs showed a reversible intercalation mechanism in the potential window of 0.5-3 V, in which the nanowire-framework is well maintained.  In the latter case, the interlayers of WS2 are gradually expanded and exfoliated during repeated charge-discharge cycling.  This not only provides more active sites and open channels for the intercalation of Na+ but also facilitates the electronic and ionic diffusion.  Therefore, WS2 NWs exhibited an ultra-long cycle life with high capacity and rate capability in the potential window of 0.5-3 V.  This study shows that WS2 NWs are promising as the anode materials of room-temp. SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqC-krHnyYYqrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgbKbdEuUEHtA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtFWgtb7F&amp;md5=2933590e4f46f62cc7a2a8a114b4935b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref16"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref16" class="rightTabRefNumLink">16</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit16" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.6b00179"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Du, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xiong, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cui, G.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Nickel Disulfide-Graphene Nanosheets Composites with Improved Electrochemical Performance for Sodium Ion Battery</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Appl.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">As an alternative system of rechargeable Li-ion batteries, Na-ion batteries revitalize researchers' interest due to the low cost, abundant Na resources, and similar storage mechanism to Li ion batteries.  VS4 has emerged as a promising anode material for SIBs due to low cost and its unique linear chains structure that can offer potential sites for Na storage.  Herein, the authors present the growth of VS4 on reduced graphene oxide (rGO) as SIBs anode for the 1st time.  The VS4/rGO anode exhibits promising performance in SIBs.  It delivers a reversible capacity of 362 mA h g-1 at 100 mA g-1 and a good rate performance.  The authors also study the Na storage behavior of the VS4/rGO.  Different than most transition metal sulfides, the VS4/rGO composite experiences a 3-step sepn. mechanism during the sodiation process (VS4 to metallic V and Na2S, then the electrochem. mechanism is akin to Na-S).  The VS4/rGO composite proves to be a promising material for rechargeable SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpiEKpa0_88WbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgbKbdEuUEHtA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsVeqsb3K&amp;md5=1bd6b7b28b6875016174fb475c0a70f3</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref18" class="rightTabRefNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit18" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2016.01.092"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sun, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Rui, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jiang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sun, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Dou, S.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Bismuth Sulfide: a High-Capacity Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sb-C nanofibers are synthesized successfully through a single-nozzle electrospinning technique and subsequent calcination. Electrochem. expts. show that the Sb-C nanofiber electrode can deliver large reversible capacity (631 mA h g-1) at C/15, greatly improved rate capability (337 mA h g-1 at 5 C) and excellent cycling stability (90% capacity retention after 400 cycles).         </div><div class="casAbstract">Lithium ion batteries exhibit high energy and power densities, thereby making them a promising power sources for multifarious applications.  However, the abundance of lithium (Li) is one of the major crit. issues for using Li battery technologies.  Therefore, for large-scale applications a sodium (Na) ion battery is one of the apt alternatives for portable electronics instead of expensive Li ion batteries.  One of the challenging issues in Na+ ion batteries is the difficulty to understand the chem. involved in view of the large size of the Na+ ion as compared to the Li+ ion, which makes the alloying/dealloying difficult during cycling.  Hence, in this present work, we explore an innovative concept of storing Na+ ions in reduced graphene oxide/antimony (Sb) metal composites.  Such a concept of storing Na+ in the rGO/Sb composite is one of the simplest ways to enhance the electrochem. performance of metal-based anodes for sodium ion batteries.  Furthermore, it is seen that the nano rGO sheet transforms to nanoribbons upon galvanostatic cycling, as evidenced by TEM.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGryp-lzHn0P9rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj-eVxeiykEtw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhtVWrtbbF&amp;md5=0cb4120ef4c51ee603ae519957bf98c0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref30" class="rightTabRefNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit30" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2015.01.092"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, Z.-J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, Y.-X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chou, S.-L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, H.-J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, H.-K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, J.-Z.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Rapid Synthesis of α-Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO Nanocomposites by Microwave Autoclave as Superior Anodes for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.                         rightTab-cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">VO2/rGO nanorods as a potential anode for sodium- and lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">He, Guang; Li, Longjun; Manthiram, Arumugam</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">28</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">14750-14758</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">VO2 (B) is an interesting cathode candidate in lithium-ion batteries with a high theor. capacity and fast charge/mass transfer rate.  Most of the studies on this material have focused on the lithium insertion reaction in the range of 4.0-1.0 V.  In this paper, VO2/rGO nanocomposite was prepd. by a microwave-assisted solvothermal method and investigated in both lithium-ion and sodium-ion batteries as a potential anode.  The VO2 (B) nanorods have an av. diam. of ∼200 nm, and is encapsulated by reduced graphene oxide (rGO) nanosheets.  Electrochem. results reveal that the VO2/rGO electrodes exhibit stable cycling and good rate performance in both Li and Na cells.  Reversible capacities of 400 mA h g-1 over 400 cycles (vs. Li/Li+) and 200 mA h g-1 over 200 cycles (vs. Na/Na+) have been achieved, indicating it is potential as an anode candidate either in lithium- or sodium-ion batteries.  Nevertheless, the reaction mechanisms seem to be different in Li and Na cells.  The crystal structure of VO2 (B) is maintained at a low discharge potential of 0.05 V in lithium-ion cells, while phase amorphization occurs in sodium-ion cells below 0.5 V.  This result is consistent with the previous study on TiO2, further confirming that some stable metal oxides may show rather different behaviors in Na cells than expected.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo5rtd1GvwU2bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liqBqLTX49uNg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtFSksrzL&amp;md5=58cecc88180fdde5de03e7ad9905bed0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref35"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref35" class="rightTabRefNumLink">35</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit35" data-doi="10.1039/C3CC47977C"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jian, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhao, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zheng, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Shi, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, H.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> Nanocrystals Anchored onto Graphene Nanosheets as the Anode Material for Low-Cost Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Chem.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The status of ambient temp. sodium ion batteries is reviewed in light of recent developments in anode, electrolyte and cathode materials.  These devices, although early in their stage of development, are promising for large-scale grid storage applications due to the abundance and very low cost of sodium-contg. precursors used to make the components.  The engineering knowledge developed recently for highly successful Li ion batteries can be leveraged to ensure rapid progress in this area, although different electrode materials and electrolytes will be required for dual intercalation systems based on sodium.  In particular, new anode materials need to be identified, since the graphite anode, commonly used in lithium systems, does not intercalate sodium to any appreciable extent.  A wider array of choices is available for cathodes, including high performance layered transition metal oxides and polyanionic compds.  Recent developments in electrodes are encouraging, but a great deal of research is necessary, particularly in new electrolytes, and the understanding of the SEI films.  The engineering modeling calcns. of Na-ion battery energy d. indicate that 210 Wh kg-1 in gravimetric energy is possible for Na-ion batteries compared to existing Li-ion technol. if a cathode capacity of 200 mAh g-1 and a 500 mAh g-1 anode can be discovered with an av. cell potential of 3.3 V.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGojsFXLPEQzILVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liqBqLTX49uNg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XntlSnurc%253D&amp;md5=fa5d7d089d261a40896cb6b03e88bfbe</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref37"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref37" class="rightTabRefNumLink">37</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit37" data-doi="10.1039/C4EE03759F"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cheng, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Pyrite FeS<sub>2</sub> for High-Rate and Long-Life Rechargeable Sodium Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Energy Environ.                         rightTab-cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Pyrite FeS2 for high-rate and long-life rechargeable sodium batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hu, Zhe; Zhu, Zhiqiang; Cheng, Fangyi; Zhang, Kai; Wang, Jianbin; Chen, Chengcheng; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">It is desirable to develop electrode materials for advanced rechargeable batteries with low cost, long life, and high-rate capability.  Pyrite FeS2, as an easily obtained natural mineral, has been already commercialized in primary lithium batteries, but encountered problems in rechargeable batteries with carbonate-based electrolytes due to the limited cycle life caused by the conversion-type reaction (FeS2 + 4M → Fe + 2M2S (M = Li or Na)).  Herein, we demonstrate that FeS2 microspheres can be applied in room-temp. rechargeable sodium batteries with only the intercalation reaction by simultaneously selecting a compatible NaSO3CF3/diglyme electrolyte and tuning the cut-off voltage to 0.8 V.  A surprisingly high-rate capability (170 mA h g-1 at 20 A g-1) and unprecedented long-term cyclability (∼90% capacity retention for 20 000 cycles) has been obtained.  We suggest that a stable elec. conductive layer-structured NaxFeS2 was formed during cycling, which enables the highly reversible sodium intercalation and deintercalation.  Moreover, 18650-type sodium batteries were constructed exhibiting a high capacity of ∼4200 mA h (corresponding to 126 W h kg-1 and 382 W h L-1) and a capacity retention of 97% after an initial 200 cycles at 4 A during charge-discharge.  This shows that the prodn. of rechargeable sodium batteries with FeS2 microspheres is viable for com. utilization.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrFxqeM-EGKh7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liqBqLTX49uNg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhs1arsL0%253D&amp;md5=25c3d019d88687effcc5109727ee9bce</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref38" class="rightTabRefNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit38" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201501785"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Su, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kretschmer, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, G.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Improved Electrochemical Performance of Na-Ion Batteries in Ether-Based Electrolytes: A Case Study of ZnS Nanospheres</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The use is demonstrated of FeSe2 as an anode material for sodium-ion batteries.  The FeSe2 microspheres assembled by nanooctahedra display a high tapping d. of 1.85 g cm-3 and a discharge capacity of 447 mA h g-1 at 0.1 A g-1.  The FeSe2 anode also exhibits long-term cyclic stability (372 mA h g-1 with capacity retention of 89.0% after 2000 cycles at 1 A g-1 ) and excellent high-rate performance 388 mA h g-1 at 10 C, 337 mA h g-1 at 20 C, 226 mA h g-1 at 50 C, where 1 C = 0.5 A g-1.  The conversion reaction of FeSe2 + 4Na+ + 4e ↔ Fe + 2Na2Se has been confirmed.  Furthermore, the FeSe2 anode is coupled with an excessive Na3V2(PO4)3 cathode (the capacity of the Na3V2(PO4)3 is 1.5-2 times more than that of FeSe2) to fabricate a full cell, which exhibits a discharge capacity of 366 mA h g-1 based on the mass of FeSe2 with an av. output voltage of about 1.7 V at 1 A g-1.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqNZQmIWuA02rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liqBqLTX49uNg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXmslens7Y%253D&amp;md5=0ecc7e52e3b809d3dadbf828186e0859</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref40"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref40" class="rightTabRefNumLink">40</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit40" data-doi="10.1039/c3ra46956e"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">MoS2-reduced graphene oxide (RGO) composites were successfully synthesized via microwave-assisted redn. of graphite oxide in a MoS2 precursor aq. soln. using a microwave system.  The morphol., structure and photocatalytic performance in the degrdn. of methylene blue (MB) were characterized by SEM, X-ray diffraction, electrochem. impedance spectra and UV-vis absorption spectroscopy, resp.  The results show that the MoS2-RGO composites exhibit enhanced photocatalytic performance in the degrdn. of MB with a max. degrdn. rate of 99% under visible light irradn. for 60 min.         </div><div class="casAbstract">GeO2-reduced graphene oxide (RGO) composites were prepd. by a simple freeze-drying method.                         rightTab-cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Porous CuO nanowires as the anode of rechargeable Na-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Lijiang; Zhang, Kai; Hu, Zhe; Duan, Wenchao; Cheng, Fangyi; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Research</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">We report the prepn. of porous CuO nanowires that are composed of nanoparticles (∼50 nm) via a simple decompn. of a Cu(OH)2 precursor and their application as the anode materials of rechargeable Na-ion batteries.  The as-prepd. porous CuO nanowires exhibit a Brunauer-Emmett-Teller (BET) surface area of 13.05 m2·g-1, which is six times larger than that of bulk CuO (2.16 m2·g-1).  The anode of porous CuO nanowires showed discharge capacities of 640 mA·h·g-1 in the first cycle and 303 mA·h·g-1 after 50 cycles at 50 mA·g-1.  The high capacity is attributed to porous nanostructure which facilitates fast Na-intercalation kinetics.  The mechanism of electrochem. Na-storage based on conversion reactions has been studied through cyclic voltammetry, X-ray diffraction (XRD), Raman spectroscopy, and high resoln. transmission electron microscopy (HRTEM).  It is demonstrated that in the discharge process, Na+ ions first insert into CuO to form a Cu1-xIICuxIO1-x/2 solid and a Na2O matrix then Cu1-xIICuxIO1-x/2 reacts with Na+ to produce Cu2O, and finally Cu2O decomp. into Cu nanoparticles enclosed in a Na2O matrix.  During the charge process, Cu nanoparticles are first oxidized to generate Cu2O and then converted back to CuO.  This result contributes to the design and mechanistic anal. of high-performance anodes for rechargeable Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrxvWXcK-rpArVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh2xWRQwZv2Sg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhvFyltbbO&amp;md5=07cf7e146303cae03a93a1846b17d7bd</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref46" class="rightTabRefNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit46" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2016.04.042"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yuan, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Huang, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yin, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, L.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Facile Synthesis of CuS/rGO Composite with Enhanced Electrochemical Lithium-Storage Properties through Microwave-Assisted Hydrothermal Method</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Electrochim.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Cu sulfide nanoflower/reduced graphene oxide (CuS/rGO) composite was synthesized using Cu(NO3)2, thiourea (Tu) and graphene oxide (GO) powers as the precursor by an ultrafast microwave-assisted hydrothermal method.  The electrochem. performances of CuS/rGO composite as anode material of Li ion batteries (LIBs) were studied both in ether-based (LiTFSI in DOL/DME) and carbonate-based electrolytes (LiPF6 in EC/DMC).  CuS/rGO composite exhibits excellent electrochem. Li-storage properties.  The reversible capacity of 422 mA h g-1 and 390 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1 after 70 cycles was obtained in both electrolytes, resp.  Even after 200 charge-discharge cycles at 500 mA g-1 in ether-based electrolyte, the composite delivers a good discharge capacity of 390 mA h g-1 with high capacity retention ratio of 96.7%.  The good electrochem. performances of CuS/rGO can be attributed to the synergistic effect of the CuS nanoflower and rGO.  Briefly, the introduction of rGO can improve the electronic cond. of the composite, effectively immobilize the CuS and inhibit the dissoln. of the polysulfide intermediates generated during the charge-discharge process.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqMymmXOZ2BKbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh2xWRQwZv2Sg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XmtFeksb8%253D&amp;md5=ef777b29f430f7ddde86f541c0098d9e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref47"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref47" class="rightTabRefNumLink">47</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit47" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201403734"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jache, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Adelhelm, P.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Use of Graphite as a Highly Reversible Electrode with Superior Cycle Life for Sodium-Ion Batteries by Making Use of Co-Intercalation Phenomena</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Angew.                 <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ACIEF5</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1433-7851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Although being the std. anode material in Li-ion batteries (LIBs), graphite so far is considered to fail application in Na-ion batteries (NIBs) because the Na-C system lacks suitable binary intercalation compds.  This limitation can be circumvented by using co-intercalation phenomena in a diglyme-based electrolyte.  The resulting compd. is a stage-I ternary intercalation compd. with an estd. stoichiometry of Na(diglyme)2C20.  Highlights of the electrode reaction are its high energy efficiency, the small irreversible loss during the 1st cycle, and a superior cycle life with capacities close to 100 mA-h g-1 for 1000 cycles and coulomb efficiencies &gt;99.87%.  A 1-to-one comparison with the analog Li-based cell shows that the Na-based system performs better and also withstands higher currents.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrIP5gn46fMJLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh2xWRQwZv2Sg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXht1WlsbbE&amp;md5=80e4b709236b714939a54f259d959661</span></div></div></div></div></li></ol></li><li id="pane-m3" aria-labelledby="pane-m3" class="tab__pane tab__pane-suppInfo"><h2 class="supp-info-label">Supporting Information</h2><div class="article_supporting-info" id="rightTab-notes-2"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="rightTab-_i8">Supporting Information</h2></div></div></div><hr><p class="last">The Supporting Information is available free of charge on the <a href="/" class="ext-link">ACS Publications website</a> at DOI: <a href="/doi/abs/10.1021/acsami.6b12529" class="ext-link">10.1021/acsami.6b12529</a>.</p><ul class="NLM_list-list_type-label" id="silist"><li><p class="inline">Text giving the TGA curves, SAED patterns, and CE of the samples (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.6b12529/suppl_file/am6b12529_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">PDF</a>)</p></li></ul><p></p><div class="supInfoBoxOnFTP "><div class="sup-info-attachments"><ul><li><a class="suppl-anchor" href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.6b12529/suppl_file/am6b12529_si_001.pdf">am6b12529_si_001.pdf (541.22 kb)</a></li></ul></div></div><div id="rightTab-figshare-widget"></div><br><div class="TermsAndConditionsDropzoneRight" data-pb-dropzone="TermsAndConditionsDropzoneRight"><div data-widget-def="UX3HTMLWidget" data-widget-id="b84e6b6c-b4d0-4427-b286-3cf14d52d013" class="mb-4">

        <script nonce="90f6e7e75ed6775c-LHR">
(function(){
	
	/*Event Tracking for RIS menu dropdown - Article pages*/

	$('.cit-download-dropdown_button').on('click',function(e)
	{	
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':'Main'});

	});


	$('.cit-download-dropdown_content ul li').on('click',function(e)
	{	
	//	e.preventDefault();
	    var idx = $(this).index();
	    
	    var label = '';
	    if (idx === 0 ) {
	    	label = 'Citation';
	    } else if (idx === 1 ) {
	    	label = 'Abstract';
	    } else if (idx === 2 ) {
	    	label = 'Reference';
	    } else if (idx === 3 ) {
	    	label = 'More Options';
	    }
	   
	   gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':label});
	});

	$('.header_contnav-next a').on('click', function(e){
        e.preventDefault();
        gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Right Arrow'});
	}); 

 	$('.header_contnav-pre a').on('click', function(e){
	    e.preventDefault();
	     gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Left Arrow'});
	}); 

	$('.share_button').on('click', function(e){
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Share'});
	});

	$("#pane-m1con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Figures'});
	});

	$("#pane-m2con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'References'});
	});

	$("#pane-m3con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Supporting Info'});
	});

	$('.tab__close').on('click', function(){
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Close'});
	}); 



})();

</script>

<script nonce="90f6e7e75ed6775c-LHR">
    document.addEventListener("DOMContentLoaded", function(){
    // Function to get a Human readable formatted date
    function getFormattedDateForMaintenance() {
        let today = new Date();
        let dd = String(today.getDate()).padStart(2, '0');
        //January is 0
        let mm = String(today.getMonth() + 1).padStart(2, '0'); 
        let yyyy = today.getFullYear();
        
        let daysOfWeek = ['Sunday', 'Monday', 'Tuesday', 'Wednesday', 'Thursday', 'Friday', 'Saturday'];
        let monthsOfYear = ['January', 'February', 'March', 'April', 'May', 'June', 'July', 'August', 'September', 'October', 'November', 'December'];

        let dayOfWeek = daysOfWeek[today.getDay()];
        let monthOfYear = monthsOfYear[today.getMonth()];

        return dayOfWeek + ', ' + monthOfYear + ' ' + dd + ', ' + yyyy;
    }
    
    // Insert the date into the .system-message-date element
    document.querySelector('.system-message-date').innerText = getFormattedDateForMaintenance();
});
</script>

<script type="text/javascript" nonce="90f6e7e75ed6775c-LHR">
"use strict"
//Script checks gdpr cookie and submits form
	/* 
	Create an in-page pop-up message, only for the InfoCentral homepage, that will gather email registrants for the library marketing list.

var infoCentralCapture = (function() {

    //Detect mobile device
    window.mobilecheck = function() {

u|g560|gene|gf\-5|g\-mo|go(\.w|od)|gr(ad|un)|haie|hcit|hd\-(m|p|t)|hei\-|hi(pt|ta)|hp( i|ip)|hs\-c|ht(c(\-| |_|a|g|p|s|t)|tp)|hu(aw|tc)|i\-(20|go|ma)|i230|iac( |\-|\/)|ibro|idea|ig01|ikom|im1k|inno|ipaq|iris|ja(t|v)a|jbro|jemu|jigs|kddi|keji|kgt( |\/)|klon|kpt |kwc\-|kyo(c|k)|le(no|xi)|lg( g|\/(k|l|u)|50|54|\-[a-w])|libw|lynx|m1\-w|m3ga|m50\/|ma(te|ui|xo)|mc(01|21|ca)|m\-cr|me(rc|ri)|mi(o8|oa|ts)|mmef|mo(01|02|bi|de|do|t(\-| |o|v)|zz)|mt(50|p1|v )|mwbp|mywa|n10[0-2]|n20[2-3]|n30(0|2)|n50(0|2|5)|n7(0(0|1)|10)|ne((c|m)\-|on|tf|wf|wg|wt)|nok(6|i)|nzph|o2im|op(ti|wv)|oran|owg1|p800|pan(a|d|t)|pdxg|pg(13|\-([1-8]|c))|phil|pire|pl(ay|uc)|pn\-2|po(ck|rt|se)|prox|psio|pt\-g|qa\-a|qc(07|12|21|32|60|\-[2-7]|i\-)|qtek|r380|r600|raks|rim9|ro(ve|zo)|s55\/|sa(ge|ma|mm|ms|ny|va)|sc(01|h\-|oo|p\-)|sdk\/|se(c(\-|0|1)|47|mc|nd|ri)|sgh\-|shar|sie(\-|m)|sk\-0|sl(45|id)|sm(al|ar|b3|it|t5)|so(ft|ny)|sp(01|h\-|v\-|v )|sy(01|mb)|t2(18|50)|t6(00|10|18)|ta(gt|lk)|tcl\-|tdg\-|tel(i|m)|tim\-|t\-mo|to(pl|sh)|ts(70|m\-|m3|m5)|tx\-9|up(\.b|g1|si)|utst|v400|v750|veri|vi(rg|te)|vk(40|5[0-3]|\-v)|vm40|voda|vulc|vx(52|53|60|61|70|80|81|83|85|98)|w3c(\-| )|webc|whit|wi(g |nc|nw)|wmlb|wonu|x700|yas\-|your|zeto|zte\-/i.test(a.substr(0,4))) check = true;})(navigator.userAgent||navigator.vendor||window.opera);
              return check;
        };

    var _isMobile = window.mobilecheck();
    if (_isMobile) {
        $('#gdpr-message-modal').addClass('mobile');
    }

    var emailValid = "",
        time = 3000,
        btnStatus = true,
        errorStatus = false,
        errormessage = "<p class='gdpr_err'><b>Please Enter a valid email address<b><p>";

    function init() {
        setTimeout(function() {
            var cookieExist = getCookie("gdpr");
            if (cookieExist) {
                //console.log("gdpr cookie exist");
                return false;
            } else {
                //console.log("gdpr cookie does not exist")
                gdprMessage();
            }
            //Events
            $('#closebtn').on("click", hideForm);

            //Handle submit
            $('#gdpr-message-btn').on("click", function(event) {
                handleClick();
            });

            // //Hide if clicked outside div - TO DO stop handling click after submit
            // $(document).click(function(event) {
            // 	event.stopPropagation();
            //   console.log(event.target);
            //   if (!$(event.target).closest("#gdpr-message-content").length) {
            //     $("body").find("#gdpr-message-modal").hide();
            //     $(this).off();
            //   }
            // });
            $('#gdpr-con-btn').click(function() {
                setCookie("gdpr", "true");
                hideForm();
            });
        }, time);
    }

    //Show the message
    function gdprMessage() {
        //console.log("Show GDPR Message");
        var tMessage, emailInput, messageButton, ewrap;

        $('#gdpr-message-modal').show();
    }

    function handleClick() {
        //console.log($("#gdpr-input").val());
        emailValid = validateEmail($("#gdpr-input").val());
        if (emailValid) {
            //Submit the form
            //Hide form
            if ($('.gdpr_err')) {
                $('.gdpr_err').hide();
            }

            $("#gdpr-message-content")
                //If successful then...
            setCookie("gdpr", "true");
            //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid + " submiting form");
        } else {
            //Show error message
            gdprErrorMessage();
            //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid);
        }
    }

    function gdprErrorMessage() {
        if (errorStatus) {
            return false;
        } else {
            errorStatus = true;
            $("#gdpr-message-content").append(errormessage);
        }
    }

    function validateEmail(email) {
        var re = /^(([^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+(\.[^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+)*)|(".+"))@((\[[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\])|(([a-zA-Z\-0-9]+\.)+[a-zA-Z]{2,}))$/;
        return re.test(String(email).toLowerCase());
    }

    function setCookie(name, value) {
        var expires = "";
        expires = "; expires=Fri, 31 Dec 9999 23:59:59 GMT";
        document.cookie = name + "=" + (value || "") + expires + "; path=/";
    }

    function getCookie(name) {
        var match = document.cookie.match(new RegExp(name + '=([^;]+)'));
        if (match) return match[1];
    }

    function hideForm() { //And set cookie
        $('#gdpr-message-modal').hide();
        setCookie("gdpr", "false");
        gtag('event', 'GDPR Modal', { 'event_category': 'Pubs GDPR', 'event_label':'GDPR Dismissal'});
    }

    return {
        init: init
    }
})();

$(document).ready(infoCentralCapture.init);
</script>


                    
                        



        
        <script nonce="90f6e7e75ed6775c-LHR">
var currentJournal = "ACS Applied Materials &amp;amp; Interfaces";
$(".citationLinks > a").click(function(e){
    if($(this).text() === "ACS Full Text ") {
        gtag('event', 'ACS Full Text', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Crossref") {
        gtag('event', 'Crossref', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "CAS") {
        gtag('event', 'CAS', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "PubMed") {
        gtag('event', 'PubMed', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Google Scholar") {
        gtag('event', 'Google Scholar', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).hasClass("issue-item_open-url") === true) {
        gtag('event', 'OpenURL', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
});
</script>
